In the Huangpu River

The Dahe and Jianghua Collided Yesterday Morning

Both Ships Were Damaged

Negotiations are Underway for Repairs

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Yangtze River ship Jianghua had just been repaired by the Jiangnan Shipyard and had just sailed out of the dock when it was hit by the Dada Company's Tongyang route ship Dahe. The details of the incident are recorded below:

Circumstances of the Collision: At about 9:00 AM yesterday morning, the Jianghua ship left the Jiangnan Shipyard and was scheduled to dock at the Jinliyuan Wharf to load cargo and sail to Hankou this morning. At 9:42 AM, it was near the naval buoy near the Dada Company Wharf when the Dada Company's Yangzhou route ship Dahe entered the port. At this time, the current was swift, and the captain of the Jianghua ship, in order to ensure safety, first dropped anchor there to allow the Dahe ship to turn around. Unexpectedly, the Dahe ship stopped its engines on the left front side of the Jianghua ship and quickly reversed, and its stern crashed violently into the bow of the Jianghua ship. The Jianghua ship had already dropped anchor and could not avoid the collision.

Damage: The stern of the Dahe ship swung into the bow of the Jianghua ship with great force, causing significant damage to the Jianghua ship. The wooden iron railing on the second deck was broken for 25 feet, two angle iron support pillars were broken, two drainage pipes were also broken, the lower wooden railing was broken for 15 feet, two support pillars were destroyed, and the bulwark was broken for three feet. The Dahe ship's rear stern was also seriously damaged due to the huge backwash force. The teak flat plate was destroyed, the triangular iron was cracked, and two support pillars were also broken. The collision occurred at 9:45 AM.

Entering the Shipyard for Repairs: After the accident, the Dada Company, because the Dahe ship had a scheduled voyage, first towed the Dahe into the shipyard for repairs. The company sent personnel to the Jianghua ship to inspect the damage and then sent a letter to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, stating that the Dahe was entering the port and the Jianghua was turning around, and the two ships collided because they could not avoid each other, resulting in the Dahe ship being hit by the Jianghua, and the Jianghua also suffered minor damage. The wording of the letter seemed to indicate that the responsibility for the collision lay with the Jianghua, not the Dahe.

Responsibility: After the incident, the captain of the Jianghua ship reported to the head office, stating that at 9:42 AM on this day (the 28th), the ship sailed from the Jiangnan Shipyard to the naval buoy near the Dada Wharf, and the Dahe ship entered the port with the tide. The ship first stopped to allow the Dahe ship to have enough space to turn around. Unexpectedly, the ship stopped and quickly reversed on the left front side of the ship, causing the ship to be hit (details omitted). The head office then replied to the Dada Company based on the captain's report, stating that according to the captain's report, the responsibility for the collision lies with the Dahe, and the damage to the Jianghua ship should be the responsibility of your company for repairs. This letter was sent out yesterday afternoon.

Rushing to Repair for Export: After the engineer sent by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company inspected the damage to the Jianghua, the company hired workers to urgently repair the ship to avoid delaying the voyage because the ship had to export that night. The company will also re-list the detailed repair costs in order to claim compensation from Dada. The Dahe ship is also being repaired urgently so that it will not miss its voyage.

Jianghai Customs

Commercial Goods Not Allowed to be Transported to Huludao

A Batch of Materials Transported to the Port

The Huludao port construction project is underway. One ship from the German Hengbao Company, a shipping company in Shanghai, had already been dispatched to Huludao last month, transporting over 300 tons of goods. Now, the second ship, the Shalan, arrived from Hengbao China, carrying a batch of materials for the construction of the Huludao port, which must be transshipped to the port for delivery. When the Hengbao Company dispatched the Shalan to Huludao, it added a batch of commercial goods to the ship, as the cargo space was still available. However, during customs declaration, the Jianghai Customs suddenly prohibited the transportation of passengers and goods to the island and refused to accept the declaration of goods for customs, tax collection, and loading. Only the building materials for the Huludao port construction project were allowed to be transported by the Shalan, and all other goods were refused. The company had to completely handle the withdrawal of the declaration for the goods it had contracted to transport to Huludao and transport the building materials such as hardware and rubber products to the port.

Additional Information After the Resolution of the Slaughter Tax

Corrections from the Health Bureau: In a news item in the newspapers the day before yesterday regarding the reopening of meat shops, there was a request to abolish the technician inspection fee. Inspection of slaughtered livestock is carried out to prevent epidemics and ensure the safety of meat for the sake of maintaining public health. The bureau has planned and designated multiple locations in the city for centralized slaughter in order to facilitate inspection and save expenses. The office expenses for all designated locations were originally planned to be paid by the city treasury. Later, meat shops in the Jiangwan district submitted a request to be exempted from merging with other districts for slaughter and inspection, and they were willing to share the inspection office expenses and requested that a veterinarian be assigned to inspect them on-site. The municipal government approved the request. Subsequently, meat merchants in Zhenru, Pusong, Fahua, Yangjing, Tangqiao, Gaoqiao, Yinhang, and other districts followed the precedent set by the Jiangwan district and requested to be allowed to pay the inspection office expenses and send personnel to inspect them nearby. After the bureau reported the situation to the municipal government for approval, they were allowed to pay. The funds were entirely used to offset the expenses of the inspection office. Therefore, the expenses were incurred by the meat merchants in each district requesting to set up a slaughter inspection office on-site for their own convenience, and they were approved after being reported to the municipal government. The official name and definition is actually the office expenses for the slaughter inspection office recognized by the meat shops in each district for their own convenience and cannot be called a technician inspection fee. The name and facts reported in the newspaper are very different from the established case and should be corrected in order to clarify the truth to the public. Until a method of offsetting the necessary expenses of this office is determined, it will still be difficult to abolish the expenses in order to maintain the operation of the business and should be subject to approval and implementation by the municipal government.

Procedures for Purchasing Tax Tickets: Yesterday, someone inquired about the procedures for purchasing slaughter tax tickets from the Municipal Finance Bureau. According to the Finance Bureau staff's response, the nature of the slaughter tax tickets is the same as that of stamp tax tickets, and meat merchants can purchase them from various tax collection offices at any time. Whether it is a whole book or individual sheets, there will be no mistakes as long as it is verified that they were issued by the bureau.

Pre-Slaughter Inspection Fee for Pigs

To be Collected Directly by the Finance Bureau Starting June 1st

The Shanghai Municipal Health and Finance Bureaus jointly issued a public notice yesterday stating: "It has been found that pigs transported to the concessions in the city area have been subject to pre-slaughter inspection by this Health Bureau, and an inspection fee of one dollar per pig has been collected. Zhang Baokun, the representative of the meat merchants, was previously approved to bear and pay this fee. It has now been found that the merchant's contracted period expires at the end of May of this year, and this bureau has reported it to the municipal government for approval. Starting June 1st, the collection will be directly collected by this Finance Bureau, and merchants will no longer be invited to contract. The pre-slaughter inspection fee of one dollar per pig will still be collected for each pig transported to the concession. No inspection certificate will be issued without purchasing a fee receipt."

Request to Revoke the Merchant Recognition for the County's Slaughter Tax

The County Government's Approval Order Was Not Granted

The Shanghai County Minhang Chamber of Commerce recently received a letter from the Pickled and Fresh Goods Trade Association stating that the county's slaughter tax had been contracted out to the Tongye Xiangxuetang for an annual tax amount of 2,860 yuan for Jiangsu education funds. Now, the base amount for merchant bidding is 4,000 yuan, and Wang Shoumei actually won the bid with 4,516 yuan, 6 jiao, and 6 fen. Adding the surcharge of 812 yuan, 9 jiao, 9 fen, and 9 li, the amount is almost double the original. Moreover, Wang is an outsider to the industry. Given the current poor harvest and sluggish business in various villages, Wang's high bid price will inevitably lead to harsh and excessive levies in the future.

Page 10

This will hinder the development of the industry. However, considering that the slaughter tax is related to dedicated education funds, the association is willing to undertake the tax payment according to the bid amount to avoid disturbances. Therefore, they request the government to revoke Wang Shoumei's contracted concession and allow the association to pay the tax, etc. The Chamber of Commerce immediately submitted the situation to the County Government for review. Yesterday, a decree was issued by Magistrate Yan, stating roughly that the Pickled and Fresh Goods Trade Association is deeply aware that the slaughter tax is related to dedicated education funds and is willing to undertake the payment according to the bid amount, which shows a clear understanding of righteousness and is worthy of praise. However, Wang Shoumei's bid was made in accordance with the announcement and regulations of the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office, and the office has approved the procedures. Since there is nothing improper, it is difficult to approve the request to revoke the concession. As for the collection of taxes, there are established regulations that cannot be exceeded, so there is no need to worry about disturbances.

City Chamber of Commerce

Mediating the Wharfage Dues Issue

Cotton Cloth Brokers and Merchant Guilds Attended

Negotiations Among the Three Parties Within a Week

Yesterday at 2:00 PM, the Chamber of Commerce convened a mediation session regarding the issue of wharfage dues responsibility between the cotton cloth brokerage and forwarding industries. Representatives present included Zhu Xiechen from the Forwarding Brokers Trade Association, Wu Yongxia from the Shanghai Merchant Guild Association, Wang Boxin and Yu Zizhang from the Shandong Guild Hall, Yang Junxin from the Sichuan Merchant Association, Chen Songyuan, Ke Ganchen, and Shi Jiumao from the Cotton Cloth Association. Luo Qinghua, Director of the Business Department of the City Chamber of Commerce, chaired the meeting, with Xue Guangqian as the secretary and recorder.

Discussion Summary The chairman reported the reasons for convening the meeting as ordered by the Social Affairs Bureau. First, the cotton cloth industry representative stated that there are two situations regarding cotton cloth: (1) For exports handled by merchant guilds, permits include wharfage dues, etc.; (2) For inland sales, there are no such taxes. Our industry is like a brokerage, and if we sell goods to merchant guilds, they issue permits, and the forwarding brokers handle the customs declaration. Now that the government is implementing unified taxation and the permit system has been abolished, our industry has no responsibility to pay taxes on behalf of customers. Next, the representative of the Shanghai Merchant Guild Association stated that merchant guilds are unfamiliar with the local area and entrust all matters to the forwarding agencies. Merchant guilds do not deny tax obligations. Chairman Luo Qinghua then spoke, saying that since merchant guilds have acknowledged tax obligations, there is legally no issue. The current discussion should focus on whether the cotton cloth or forwarding brokerage industry should be responsible, as the merchant guilds are unfamiliar with the local area and must entrust a third party to handle the payments. The cotton cloth industry representative reiterated the reasons why they cannot pay on behalf of customers and the convenience of having the forwarding industry do so. Representatives from the Merchant Guild Association and the forwarding industry then stated the difficulties in having the forwarding industry pay on behalf of others.

Mediation Result The chairman stated that the two sides' discussions were not close enough, and it was difficult to reach a satisfactory solution on the spot. He concluded the case, saying that the responsibility for paying wharfage dues belongs to the merchants, which is undisputed. However, the merchants are unfamiliar with the local area and must entrust a third party to handle it. Since both the cotton cloth and forwarding brokerage industries have various difficulties and are unwilling to handle it on behalf of others, it cannot be forced. There are now two proposed solutions: (1) Each representative will go back and consider the matter. Within a week, the three parties will negotiate to see if a result can be reached before reporting back to the Chamber for handling; (2) The situation of this mediation will be reported to the Social Affairs Bureau. As the representatives believed that the only point of contention was the cotton cloth and forwarding brokerage industries' obligation to pay on behalf of customers, and there was still room for joint consultation, they unanimously agreed to adopt the first solution. The chairman then announced the temporary end of the day's mediation.

Electricians

Wage and Condition Terms Re-mediated Yesterday

A Total of Nine Terms Have Been Signed and Resolved

Bonuses and Construction of Dormitories Still Need Further Negotiation

The wage and condition terms for Chinese electrical workers in this city have been repeatedly mediated by the Social Affairs Bureau without result. Yesterday was the final mediation by the Social Affairs Bureau, and the issues of bonuses and construction of dormitories remained unresolved. The details of each item are as follows:

Mediation Meeting The City Social Affairs Bureau convened the Mediation Committee again yesterday morning at 9:00 AM to re-mediate the wage and condition terms for Chinese electrical workers. Those present included Committee members Zhang Shoutao from the City Public Security Bureau, Xu Yefu from the City Party Headquarters, Yao Xinzhi and Lu Zhonglin from the Chinese Electric Company, and Zhu Hanhe and Zhou Guangrong from the First District Water and Electricity Industry Union. The meeting was chaired by Committee member Xu Zhi from the Social Affairs Bureau, with Wang Zhixin as the recorder. Until after 7:00 PM, the two sides argued most fiercely over the issues of bonuses and the construction of workers' dormitories, which could not be resolved. The chairman then announced that the two sides should negotiate separately, and if no result was reached, the committee would mediate again.

Resolved Articles The conditions that have been resolved are as follows: (1) The Chinese Electric Company (hereinafter referred to as "the Company") shall recognize that the Shanghai First District Water and Electricity Industry Union (hereinafter referred to as "the Union") has the right to represent the Union members within the Company. (2) The Company has the right to freely hire and dismiss workers, but shall not dismiss workers unless there is solid evidence of one of the following behaviors: (A) Unjustifiably causing serious injury to others; (B) Stealing public or private property; (C) Suffering from venereal disease; (D) Smoking opium; (E) Gambling during work hours; (F) Violating the Company's worker service regulations and being reprimanded nine times or receiving three major demerits within one year. The Company shall notify the Union before taking disciplinary action against workers or when workers receive major demerits. (3) The Company shall provide life insurance savings for workers. (4) (A) Adopt the New China Bank's five-year life insurance savings group savings method, and the Company shall organize a worker savings department to handle it; (B) The Company shall pay an amount equal to three and a half days' wages for each worker as the monthly life insurance savings amount for each worker, and pay it to the worker savings department on a monthly basis; (C) The worker savings department shall issue savings passbooks by name for monthly registration of savings. (4) The original retirement and pension method (as stipulated in Article 6 of the agreement agreed upon in December 1928) shall be cancelled at the end of May 1931. The Company shall calculate the number of months of retirement benefits due to each worker before the end of May 1931 according to the previous method, and the worker or the worker's family shall receive the payment calculated at the worker's last month's salary at the time of retirement or death. Those dismissed for one of the behaviors in Article 2 shall not be entitled to receive the aforementioned retirement benefits. The Company shall pay all of the retirement benefits that the worker should have received to the Worker Welfare Committee for use as Worker Welfare expenses. The Worker Welfare Committee shall be jointly formed by representatives from the Company and the Union, and the organization and detailed rules of procedure shall be separately agreed upon by both parties. (5) Medical treatment methods are stipulated as follows: (A) Hire one Western doctor and one Chinese doctor registered with the City Health Bureau to be responsible for worker medical treatment and hygiene matters on a daily basis; (B) When necessary, the Company shall send workers with illnesses (except for venereal diseases) to designated hospitals for hospitalization and treatment, and the Company shall bear the medical and other expenses; (C) The designated Chinese and Western hospitals and doctors are as follows: (A) Sacred Heart Hospital; (B) Guangci Hospital; (C) China Hospital; (D) Western Doctor Zhu Rongsheng; (E) Guoyao Hao Pengshoutang. (6) Workers who are injured or die as a result of performing their duties shall receive subsidies and pensions in accordance with the Factory Law. Those who are injured or die not as a result of performing their duties shall also receive subsidies and pensions from the Company in addition to bearing their medical expenses. The standards are stipulated as follows: (A) For workers who are temporarily unable to work due to injury or illness, a monthly subsidy equal to two-thirds of their average salary shall be given, but limited to six months; (B) For workers who are disabled due to injury or illness and permanently lose part of their ability to work, the Company shall provide light work and pay two-thirds of their original salary. Those who permanently lose all of their ability to work and are dismissed shall be given a subsidy equal to one-half of their average salary for a period of two years, and the Company shall continue to bear their life insurance savings until the five-year term expires; (C) For deceased workers, in addition to a funeral allowance of 50 yuan, if the total amount of life insurance savings and retirement benefits before the end of May 1931 received by the deceased worker's family is less than 300 yuan and two years' average salary, the Company shall make up the difference. (7) The 200 yuan per month subsidy to the Union as stipulated in the previous agreement shall be cancelled at the end of May 1931. Starting from June 1, the Company shall provide a one-time subsidy of 5,000 yuan for the expansion of the existing labor welfare undertakings and the establishment of labor welfare undertakings that should be established immediately, and a monthly subsidy of 600 yuan for their operating expenses. The management and use of the aforementioned funds shall be handled by the Worker Welfare Committee. (8) Matters not expressly stipulated in this agreement shall be handled in accordance with past practices and laws. If past practices are superior to laws, past practices shall be followed. If laws are superior to past practices, laws shall be followed. However, when past practices conflict with laws, laws shall still be followed. (9) The validity period of this agreement is three years, from June 1, 1931, to May 31, 1934. If either party is unwilling to continue or needs to modify it after the expiration date, it shall notify the other party in writing three months before the expiration date; otherwise, it shall be deemed to be voluntarily valid for another three years from June 1, 1934.

All Conditions for the Binding Industry Resolved

Increase Wages by One-Tenth

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Binding Workers had two strikes due to requests to improve their wage and condition terms. Most of the issues have been resolved. Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the Social Affairs Bureau convened another Mediation Committee to mediate the parts regarding wages, apprentices, and meals. Those present included Long Yinchu from the City Party Headquarters, Ding Handong and Xu Hanqing from the Union Association, and Chen Zhaoqing and Ren Changfu from the Binding Workers' Union. The meeting was chaired by Committee member Wang Bing from the Social Affairs Bureau, with Zhang Gongmu as the recorder. The mediation was concluded until after 7:00 PM. The results are recorded as follows: (1) (Wages) Wages shall be increased uniformly by one-tenth of the original amount. (2) (Apprentices) Foreign-style companies employing 10 or more workers may take in 3 apprentices. For every 5 additional workers, they may take in 1 additional apprentice, but the maximum shall not exceed 10. Chinese-style companies employing 5 or more workers may take in 1 apprentice, but the maximum shall not exceed 7. Short-term workers are not subject to this rule. (3) (Meals) Workers are free to choose their own meals and lodging. Apprentices shall follow the rules.

Unanimously Advocate Investigating Those Who Framed Them

This has been reported in various newspapers. In addition to the Anti-Drug Association's full explanation of the truth, it has been learned that anti-drug organizations in various places, such as Liaoning, Tianjin, Taiyuan, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Xinghua, Hangzhou, Suzhou, Singapore, Batavia, Jinhua, Liyang, Jining, Harbin, Xi'an, Chengdu, and dozens of other anti-drug associations and anti-drug propaganda associations, have sent letters and telegrams of condolence to Mr. and Mrs. Huang. Jiang Lugen Accused of Seduction and Fraud

A Woman from Changzhou, Zhu, Recently Entrusted Lawyer Fan Gang and Fan Qisheng to File a Lawsuit with the Special District Court Accusing Jiang Lugen of Crimes Such as Seduction and Fraud. Her Complaint Stated That the Plaintiff Was Formerly Married to Zhang Apei. Shortly After His Death, He Left Behind More Than 4,000 Yuan in Cash, Along With Clothing and Other Items Worth Nearly 10,000 Yuan. As the Second Anniversary of Her Husband's Death Approached, the Defendant Jiang Lugen Coveted Her Property and Repeatedly Tried to Seduce Her. She Initially Ignored Him, but He Persistently Harassed Her and Claimed That His Wife Had Already Run Away and That He Was Willing to Marry Her; Otherwise, He Would Ruin Her Reputation, and Her Life Would Be in Danger. Under Duress, She Immediately Cohabited with Him at 597 Kang Nao Tuo Road. It Was Said That the Defendant Was Accustomed to Vulgarity and Associated with Gangsters, Not Engaging in a Livelihood. He Relied on the Cash Left by the Plaintiff's Late Husband for Living Expenses, Extorting Money and Pawning Clothing for His Squandering. In May 1929, the Defendant Was Involved in a Kidnapping Case with Chen Jinfa and Was Detained for Five Months. After Hiring a Lawyer for Defense and Many Efforts, He Was Finally Released by the Court After It Was Determined That He Was Not Involved. Unexpectedly, After His Release, He Not Only Did Not Know to Be Grateful but, Seeing That the Plaintiff's Savings Had Been Exhausted, Intended to Abandon Her. He Became Violent and Beat Her. She Was Forced to Return to Her Mother's Home to Demand Repayment of the Advance Payments. Although He Agreed to Pay 40 Yuan Per Month for Living Expenses, He Requested a Postponement of the Repayment of the Debt. On May 16 of This Year, Because He Did Not Pay the Advance Payments and Owed Debt, She Demanded Them Strictly, Which Led Him to Hold a Grudge in His Heart. The Next Day, He Assembled Many People to Ambush Near Her Residence. When the Plaintiff Passed By, They Rushed Out and Injured Her Head with Weapons, Creating Two Holes About an Inch Deep. Her Waist, Arms, and Other Parts of Her Body Were Also Severely Injured. She Immediately Reported This to the Nearby Songshan Road Police Station, Which Sent Her to Renji Hospital for Treatment. His Actions Showed That He Intended to Take Advantage of Her Wealth, Seduce Her, Commit Adultery, Abandon Her After Her Money Was Exhausted, and Even Assemble a Crowd to Beat Her, Intending to Kill Her, Which Violated Articles 285 and 363 of the Criminal Law. She Requested That He Be Punished According to Law and That Her Clothing and Silver Dollars Be Recovered. After Receiving the Lawsuit, the Court Has Issued Summonses for Both Parties to Appear and Will Open a Hearing Tomorrow.

A Sudden Love Letter

Almost Cost Wang Axi Her Life

Lu Azhong, also known as Lu Xiutao, 28 years old, from Ningbo, lives at 242 Renyu Lane, Baochang Road, Baoshan Road, Zhabei. He is an employee on the Japanese ship Nanyang Maru. His wife, Wang Axi, 22 years old, also from Ningbo, is a worker in a cigarette factory. They have a daughter named Lianying, who is only 5 years old. Recently, Lu suspected that his wife Wang was having an affair with someone else, which caused discord between the couple, and they often argued and fought. Unexpectedly, the other day, a letter signed by Sheng Laiming arrived. The envelope was addressed to Wang Axi and was marked as sent from Tianjin, but the postmark on the stamp clearly showed Shanghai. Azhong received the letter and opened it. The content was roughly as follows: "After our love affair began, I originally intended to remain consistent to the end. However, your husband has learned of it and has abused you in every way. I really can't bear it. I will cut off all ties of love from now on so that your couple can remain as good as before," and so on. After reading it, Azhong believed that this was solid evidence and beat his wife severely without asking for the reason, saying, "If you don't truthfully confess your lover, I will definitely take your life with an ax tonight." Overwhelmed with anger, Wang was so upset that she wished she were dead. In the evening, when Azhong went out, Wang took the opportunity to leave, heading south on North Henan Road. Unexpectedly, her husband chased after her, cursing as he ran. When they reached Tianhou Palace Bridge, Lu shouted, "Your death place has arrived! Die quickly! Die quickly!" Wang became even more angry and jumped into the river from the wharf of the nearby post office to seek death. Others saw what happened and wanted to save her, but Lu firmly blocked them. Fortunately, Hua, a patrolman named Xunjiang from the Customs Water Police Station, passed by and immediately rescued her. Because it was not too late, her life was not in danger. She was taken to the police station, where she confessed the details. The police station ordered detective Huang Songsheng to investigate and brought her husband to the police station to be detained on the charge of forcing his wife to commit suicide, pending transfer to the court for trial. Yesterday morning, her sister came to the station to request permission to mediate. She repeatedly explained the advantages and disadvantages to Lu. Hearing this, Lu suddenly realized his past mistakes and cried with his wife, asking for reconciliation on the spot. The police chief approved the dismissal of the prosecution and ordered the original detective to transfer the couple to the Fifth District Public Security Bureau for disposition.

Chinese Concession Telephone Monthly Rent

Entrusting Shanghai Bank to Collect Payments

Old Beggar Is a Thief

Pretending to Be Sick Lying at the Back Door

Zhao Fushou Is a Habitual Thief

Chen Zhongbao, 19 years old, and Feng Gu, 20 years old, from Ningbo, are currently studying at the Southeast Medical College of the Shanghai Army Camp in Nanshi and reside together at No. 121 Nanjing Street near the school. At about 6:00 AM on the 26th of this month, Chen and Feng got up one after the other and went to school together. As soon as they left the door, they suddenly saw an old beggar sleeping at the back door, but they did not pay much attention to him. When they returned from school, Wang Yucai, their fellow villager who lived with them, suddenly said, "When you went to school, you didn't close the back door after leaving, which caused a thief to break into my home and steal more than a dozen items, including my clothes, thermos, and sundries. But you should be responsible for this matter." Chen and others realized that the old beggar they saw at the back door in the morning must have been the thief. By this time, there was no trace of him, and they had to admit their bad luck and agreed to compensate for the loss. Until about 4:00 AM yesterday, Zhang Shishi, 41 years old, from Tongzhou, who lived in the house next door at No. 123, was selling fruit. At that time, Zhang sent his daughter out because of something, and when he stepped out of the door, he suddenly saw an old beggar lying on the back door steps, moaning incessantly, looking as if he was ill. At that time, he was not surprised, so he turned around and left. Not long after Zhang returned home and entered the bedroom, he saw the sick beggar who had been lying on the steps suddenly carrying two brass teapots belonging to his family, poking his head and looking around. He realized that he was a thief and immediately jumped up, grabbed him tightly, and shouted "Thief!" Chen Zhongbao, Feng Gu, Wang Yucai, and others also heard the sound and rushed to Zhang's house next door. They saw that the thief Zhang had caught was the old beggar they had seen sleeping at the back door last time. At this time, they were extremely angry and immediately went out and reported to Wu Shutang, the guard on duty at the 22nd post, who brought the thief to the First Branch of the First District Police Station. During the preliminary interrogation by the director of the station, the thief confessed that his name was Zhao Fushou, 57 years old, from Shaoxing, and that he was staying at the Fuxinggong Inn in Laobeimen, Minguo Road. He used to make a living by selling tofu and dried bean curd. Because the profit from that business was too small, he had no choice but to resort to this tactic, pretending to be a sick beggar and sleeping on the steps of the back doors of the surrounding residents, taking the opportunity to break in and steal things when people were unprepared. He was ordered to be detained for further investigation.

Petition to Dredge the Putan

Xing Zhigang and Other Representatives of the Shipping Households in the Shanghai South District Believe That the Putan Along the Folk Boat Wharves in Nanshi Is Becoming Increasingly Silty, Obstructing Transportation and Harming Commerce. Yesterday, They Jointly Submitted a Petition to the Municipal Government Requesting Dredging to Facilitate Transportation. The Petition Stated That the Dredging of Shallow Beaches Along the River Is Requested to Facilitate Transportation. Since the Wharves Along the Coast of Nanshi Were Taken Over by the City, Except for the Steamboat Wharves, Which Have the Public Works Bureau Establish a Management Office, the Boat Docks from Wanyu Wharf to Santai Wharf Have Not Been Dredged for Several Years, Resulting in the Increasing Silting of the Putan. It Is Difficult for Cargo Ships Arriving from Various Roads in the Urban Area to Dock and Unload. In Addition, Bamboo and Wood Businesses Along the Coast Use the Putan as a Place to Store Materials, Stacking Them Higher and Higher Without Limits. There Are Also Many Junks Occupying the Shallow Beaches Along the Coast, Using Them as Homes, Which Makes It Easier for Water, Sand, and Mud Brought by the Tide to Accumulate. The Shallow Beaches on the Side of the Putan Are Widening, and the Shipping Lanes in the Putan Are Narrowing Day by Day, Which Obstructs the Sailing of Folk Boats and Steamships. Previously, It Was Reported That the Wharf Management Office of the City Public Works Bureau, in View of the Deep Accumulation of Mud on the Putan Surface of Various Steamboat Wharves, Which Hinders the Navigation of Ships and Affects the Losses of Merchants, Had Informed the Municipal Government to Find Ways to Dredge It, and It Is Reported That Approval Has Been Granted. Recently, They Are Actively Consulting with the Dredging Bureau and Will Soon Be Able to Implement Dredging. Since the Steamboat Wharves Already Have the Public Works Bureau Responsible for Dredging, the Part of the Folk Boat Wharves Should Also Be Regarded as the Same. It Is Found That the Cargo Ship Registration Statistics Last Month Reached More Than 8,600, and the Monthly Boat Donation Revenue Is About 18,000 Silver Dollars, Which Is More Than Sufficient to Maintain the Wharf. However, the Shallow Beaches South of Wanyu Wharf Have Never Been Dredged or Built as a Wharf, Which Makes It Difficult for Cargo Ships Arriving in Shanghai to Dock and Makes It Difficult to Load and Unload Cargo Far in the Center of the River. It Is Thought That Wanyu, Gongyi, Dongjiadu, and the South Hall Wharves Are the Most Prosperous Areas for Ships from the Four Townships and Are the Commercial Center of the Coast of Nanshi. Now That the Public Works Bureau Has Been Approved by Your Government to Contact the Dredging Bureau to Dredge the Steamship Wharves, the Adjacent Folk Boat Wharves Are Also Under the Rule of Your Government and Fulfill the Obligation of Paying Taxes. They Should Be Planned and Dredged Together. Therefore, They Jointly Submit This Petition to Your Seat, Requesting That You Approve and Order the Public Works Bureau to Plan and Carry Out the Dredging of the Folk Boat Wharves and the Steamship Wharves at the Same Time to Benefit Shipping and Avoid Partiality. They Will Be Grateful Beyond Measure.

Inciting Prostitution Lawsuit

Two defendants filed a counterclaim

Lawyer requested to examine Han Village

Li Xuru, a woman from Beiping, graduated from a normal university in Japan in her early years. After graduation, she founded the Modern Times in Tianjin and established a school in Beiping. Her husband, Kong Ren, is currently employed in Guangdong. Recently, Li, along with Chen Yindi, a 13-year-old girl from Yangzhou, retained lawyer Ye Fukan to file a criminal lawsuit with the Special District Local Court against Yao Zhang (43 years old), the wife of the deceased famous actor Yao Junqing from Beiping, who lives at No. 18 Jiufu Lane, Mengdelan Road, and is a shareholder of the former Grand Theater, and her daughter Yao Shunxi (also known as Yuqin, 21 years old) for obstructing public morals and other offenses. The following is a record of the situation:

The plaintiff's complaint is for abducting and escaping, and for seducing and raping a virgin. They requested that the case be arrested and severely punished, and that the person be handed over. The first plaintiff, Li Xuru, married Ren Shuzhen (now named Yanhua) in Beiping at a high price. In October of the 19th year of the Republic, she took her to Shanghai and lived upstairs with the defendants. Who knew that the defendant's mother and daughter were famous salted meat dealers in Northern Shanghai, and they often took Shuzhen out to play. At first, they did not feel strange. Later, the plaintiff left Shanghai in mid-November of the same year, leaving only Shuzhen, the second concubine, Ms. Gao, and Ms. Gao's mother, Ms. Tian, in Shanghai. When the plaintiff returned to Shanghai in March of the second year of the Republic, it was only a few days. Unexpectedly, the defendants had seduced Shuzhen, abducted her without a trace, and seized more than a thousand yuan of clothing and accessories. After investigation, Chen, the daughter of a tenant downstairs, Yindi (the second plaintiff), said that after the plaintiff left Shanghai, the defendant's mother and daughter often took Shuzhen and Yindi out. Every time they went, they would first go to the concubine's house of the front desk manager of the Shanghai Theater to change into grand clothes and go to the No. 1 Lian Sheng Fang salted meat store on Changbang Road to introduce customers and arrange prostitution. This abduction must be the instigator, and Yao Zhang and her daughter also tricked Chen Yindi into going to the salted meat store to receive customers at the same time. Because she refused, she was not harmed, etc. When asked about Ms. Lao Si, a neighbor, she also said that the defendants often lured Shuzhen to the salted meat store to introduce prostitution. Now that Shuzhen has fled, the defendant is definitely the instigator. The facts are obvious. The defendants' previous actions violated Article 246 of the Criminal Law. It seems that this kind of luring good women to salted meat stores for adultery is a common business, and the victims are too numerous to count. How much harm does it cause to public morals? Therefore, I ask your court to quickly arrest the defendants and punish them severely according to the law, and order them to hand over the victim, Shuzhen, and the clothes and accessories worth more than a thousand yuan attached to the civil lawsuit, and order them to be recovered to uphold the law and punish the wicked.

Defendant's defense: The court approved the application and issued a summons a few days ago to arrest and inform them. When the time came to surrender to await interrogation, Yao Zhang and Yao Shunxi also retained lawyers Fan Gang and Fan Qisheng. In addition to defending according to the law, they also claimed that Li Xuru and others' accusations were completely false. They also filed a counterclaim accusing Li Xuru and Chen Yindi of slander and damage to their reputation. Their counterclaim is recorded below as a notification to defend according to the law and file a counterclaim, requesting that they be severely punished to deter slander and protect their reputation. The first defendant and counterclaimant, Yao Zhang, is the wife of the deceased famous actor Yao Junqing, the former shareholder of the Grand Theater. She has lived in Shanghai with her husband and daughter Shunxi for many years. She inherited her late husband's property and can barely make ends meet. She has never engaged in illegal activities. The two counterclaim defendants rented the defendant's remaining house in succession in 18 years of the Republic. Because of the pursuit of rent arrears and other facts, they each had grievances in their hearts and dared to collude and fabricate facts to falsely accuse them, causing the counterclaimant's reputation to suffer significant damage. The reasons are described below: "Defense Part" According to the plaintiff, the defendant and counterclaimant is a famous dealer of salted meat shops in Northern Shanghai, usually taking Shuzhen out to play, and taking advantage of Li Xuru's departure from Shanghai to seduce Shuzhen and abduct her without a trace, and seize more than a thousand yuan of clothing and accessories. After investigation, Chen Yindi claimed that she and Shuzhen were often taken out by the defendant and went to the concubine's place of the front desk manager of the Shanghai Theater to change into grand clothes and go to the salted meat shop to introduce prostitution. Therefore, Shuzhen's flight this time was actually instigated by the defendant, etc. Li Xuru and her husband Kong Ren rented the defendant's wing house in October of the 18th year of the Republic with a wife and two concubines (one of whom is Shuzhen, also known as Yanhua). Chen Yindi rented the defendant's remaining house in April of the 19th year of the Republic. The relationship between the landlord and the guest is only a formality. Ren Shuzhen ran away privately in March of the 19th year. At that time, Chen Yindi had not yet met her. How could they have gone out together? Li Xuru already knew that the defendant was a famous dealer of salted meat shops. How could she allow her to often take Shuzhen out to play? Chen Yindi, again, how could she not love herself and be willing to go out with the defendant? The so-called neighbor woman named Lao Si does not exist. What is the reference to? This kind of fabricated fact has already been falsely accused. I will briefly defend and request your review. "Counterclaim Part" The reason is that Li Xuru's husband, Kong Ren, rented the counterclaimant's building in October of the 18th year of the Republic with a wife and two concubines. Seeing that the counterclaimant was a lonely widow who could be bullied, he teased the second counterclaimant, Shunxi, and hoped to make her his concubine. By March of the 19th year, Ren Shuzhen was abused and fled privately, and his lust became more intense. He dared to show frivolous behavior from time to time. Because of his humble character, he also disregarded his face and reprimanded her directly. By May, he felt ashamed and moved to another place. The original complaint falsely claimed that Ren Shuzhen was abducted and hidden without a trace in March of this year. I did not know that Shuzhen had fled in March of the 19th year and had already entrusted lawyer Zhang Yuanmei to publish a statement in July of the same year to sever the relationship between husband and concubine. The first defendant first entrusted lawyer Ye Fukan on May 13 to send a letter threatening to explain the address where Shuzhen was abducted within two days. He immediately entrusted lawyer Fan Gang to reply, ordering him to inquire with lawyer Zhang. The first defendant still falsely entrusted and filed a false accusation. As for Chen Yindi, she is the daughter of a tailor and her behavior is frivolous. She is not willing to associate with him. Because she owed rent and was pursued for loans, she harbored resentment. In March of this year, she worshiped Li as her adoptive mother. The original statement is obviously false. She is in the position of a plaintiff, but the counterclaimants are engaged in prostitution. She has been victimized. However, she is willing to sacrifice her reputation and collude with Li to damage the counterclaimants' reputation. The first counterclaimant is old and reputation is a person's second life. She cannot allow it to be sullied. The second counterclaimant is even more embarrassed as she is waiting to be married. Therefore, she filed a counterclaim (omitted below), requesting that the counterclaim defendant be punished for the crimes he deserves in accordance with Articles 180 and 324 of the Criminal Law, and ordered to publish the defense statement in the newspaper in accordance with Articles 185 and 332 of the same law to compensate for the loss of the counterclaimants' reputation.

The situation of the trial: Yesterday afternoon at 3 o'clock, Judge Luo Renji of the Special Court came to the second court to interrogate both parties. Both parties were accompanied by their lawyers. First, Judge Luo asked both parties about their age and origin. Then, lawyer Ye Fukan briefly stated the main points of the prosecution. Then, defendant's lawyer Fan Qisheng also rose to state the main points of the counterclaim and presented a newspaper with a statement published by lawyer Zhang Yuanmei on behalf of Ren Shuzhen in July of last year stating that she had severed the relationship between husband and concubine. Then, Chen Yindi complained that Yao Shunxi had repeatedly asked her to go to Zhang's residence to play and lured her to the salted meat shop, but she had noticed and escaped. However, Yao Zhang did not go with her, etc. Yao Zhang and Yao Shunxi both denied the accusations. Shunxi also confessed that she was a virgin, and the plaintiff's lawyer Ye immediately rose to declare that according to Shunxi's confession that she was still a virgin, the lawyers could ask the plaintiff to be responsible for guaranteeing that she was not a virgin and could ask the doctor to examine her. If she had a relationship with many people, she would be willing to bear the responsibility of false accusation if it was found to be untrue. The place is a famous salted meat shop. If the court wants to understand the content, it can ask to go there for inspection. Judge Luo verified the confession and announced that the case would be rescheduled for further interrogation on the afternoon of June 4 and ordered Lao Si to be summoned to court for questioning.

Due to Jealousy

Stabbed a Concubine With a Knife

Skull Shattered and Index Finger Cut Off

The Murderer Surrendered After Causing the Trouble

Confessed That It Was Caused by Extreme Hatred

The Concubine's Injuries Were Very Serious

Zhou Yueying, a woman from Ningbo, is 23 years old. In March of last year, she took a boat from her hometown to Shanghai to seek refuge with her fellow villager Ou A-Wu, intending to ask Ou to introduce her to work as a servant. Ou, who was working as a small worker at a tea shop at No. 1219 Haining Road, saw that Zhou was still young and had a beautiful appearance, so he made the excuse that Zhou was not familiar with the Shanghai dialect and it was better to live with him. The woman agreed, so they lived together and rented a house at No. 53 Houde Lane, Xiaocai Market, Yongxing Road, Zhabei, as if they were husband and wife with strong love. Two months ago, Zhou's mother suddenly came to Shanghai from Ningbo and also lived with her daughter. After only a few days, there were cracks in their relationship. On the night of the 26th of this month, Ou came home from work, but Zhou and her daughter had disappeared, and all the clothes and utensils in the room were gone. He realized that Zhou had an affair and was filled with anger, vowing to hurt her. He took a kitchen knife from his home and went to the store, secretly investigating Zhou's whereabouts. At around 3 p.m. the day before yesterday, Ou was free from work in the store, so he went for a stroll nearby and suddenly saw Zhou coming out of a movie theater. Ou ran back to the store, grabbed the kitchen knife, and hurried to chase her. He was caught up with her on North Henan Road and Aierjin Road. At that time, Zhou also knew it and hurriedly avoided into Rongqing Lane. Ou also chased in and suddenly cut Zhou's head several times with the kitchen knife. Zhou used her left hand to cover, and one section of her index finger was completely cut off. Her head was also seriously injured, and she fell to the ground in extreme pain, with blood gushing out like a spring. Ou surrendered to the Huisi Police Station with the murder weapon, stating the whole story directly. The police chief obtained the confession and immediately sent detective Wang Jie to investigate the scene. The injured person had been sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment by Indian police No. 397. Only a large pool of blood was seen in the alley, and a section of the cut-off finger was found in the blood, which was taken back to the police station. He ordered Ou to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Criminal Division 2 of the Special District Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the case, saying that Zhou was seriously injured and unable to speak at the hospital, requesting an indefinite postponement. He then presented the doctor's examination form and the murder weapon finger. The knife was stained with a lot of blood and a lock of hair. The doctor's examination form briefly stated that Zhou's head was deeply split, her skull was shattered, and her left index finger was also cut off. Her injuries were very serious, etc. The defendant admitted the previous situation and said that he was extremely angry and dizzy at the time and probably cut three or four times, etc. Judge Luo Renji verified the confession and announced that Ou Wu would be detained pending Zhou Yueying's recovery, and appointed lawyer Fan Gang as the defendant's defense lawyer in court. The murder weapon and the section of the index finger were temporarily stored in the forensic department of this court.

Coincidentally

Pockmarked Woman Requests Divorce

Because Her Face Is Pockmarked, Her Husband Dislikes Her

Two Women Should Sympathize With Each Other

Yang Zhu's Has Reconciled

Yan Zhu's Case Still Needs to Be Retried

The Shanghai Local Court accepts several divorce cases every day. The women are the majority of the petitioners, and the reasons are mostly abuse, beatings, abandonment, neglect, intention to sell, and pampering concubines and abusing wives. Yesterday, two cases of women requesting divorce were heard. The most bizarre thing is that both women have pockmarked faces, and one of the defendants disliked his wife's ugly appearance and took a concubine home to live with, and then began to abuse his wife. The other defendant also disliked his wife's unsightly appearance and had an affair with a prostitute outside and brought her home to live with. As a result, the feelings between the husband and wife were broken. The following are the details of the plaintiff's intentions and interrogations in the above two cases.

(1) Yang Zhu, a woman from Pudong, retained lawyer Shen Qi to sue her husband, Yang A-Gen, for all kinds of abuse and unbearable cohabitation. She requested a divorce and the return of her dowry and clothing, stating that she was betrothed to the defendant by her mother from a young age. At the age of 13, she went to the defendant's home as a child bride. She got married at the age of 19. At the time of the child bride and the early marriage, the parents-in-law and the defendant were still harmonious. However, in the spring of last year, the defendant had an affair with Wu Yao, the wife of Wu Xihua, and took her back to live together, as if they were husband and wife. She regarded the plaintiff as a thorn in her side and was often beaten by the defendant, the concubine, and the aunt. Moreover, she could not get enough food. The abuse became even worse. She was tied to the foot of the bed with a rope and beaten violently, causing injuries all over her body. The plaintiff called for help and was released by the superintendent Yang Huang and others. The next day, she went to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. She has a diagnosis certificate. The plaintiff applied for mediation earlier, but the defendant refused to reconcile. The defendant and his concubine habitually beat the plaintiff, and the method of beating was to tie her to the foot of the bed and make her unable to get enough food. It is truly unbearable cohabitation and should be allowed to divorce according to law. Yesterday, Judge Wang opened the court to interrogate. Yang Zhu confessed that she was 23 years old, a local and lived at the ferry crossing of Dongjiadu, Pudong. She is currently working in a cloth factory and has been married to the defendant for four years. Zhu gave birth to a child, but the defendant disliked her ugly appearance and had an affair with a woman recently and had a son. She also confessed the previous situation. According to Yang A-Gen's confession, he is 30 years old, a local and lives at No. 786 Tangqiao Town, Pudong, making a living by driving a boat. Our relationship has always been harmonious and there has never been any beating. As for my concubine, she has already been separated. I do not want to divorce. The judge obtained the confession and repeatedly advised the plaintiff that quarrels between husband and wife are common in the family. This court orders the defendant not to beat you again in the future and to separate the concubine. It is better for the husband and wife to reconcile and not divorce. The plaintiff said, what if I am beaten again? The judge said, you can come and tell me again. The plaintiff nodded, so a reconciliation was reached and the husband and wife reconciled. The judge then wrote a reconciliation record and ordered both parties to sign and leave the court. (2) Yan Zhu, a local young woman, is 24 years old this year and currently lives at No. 20 Zhujiazhai, Zhijiang Temple, Zhabei. Yan A-Wu is a local. This spring, A-Wu took a young star home to live with him. The good family has been in trouble ever since. Yan Zhu retained lawyer Yao Jian to request mediation for a divorce from the Local Court Mediation Office. The reason is that her husband, Yan A-Wu, committed bigamy and abuse. She requested a divorce and a return of alimony of 4,000 yuan (calculated at 200 yuan per year for 20 years) and a return of dowry ornaments worth 1,800 yuan. The statement stated that the defendant usually disliked her ugly appearance and often said that he would marry a beautiful woman. The defendant has more than ten acres of ancestral land, worth tens of thousands of gold. The family is quite well-off. In early February of this year, the defendant took all of her gold ornaments and sold them to marry another woman outside. On the 19th of this month, he made the Qingming Festival at home and took the woman home, clearly deceiving her weakness. Before long, she was severely beaten by the defendant and the woman. At that time, she went to the Procuratorate to verify the wounds and was advised to go home and reconcile. Unexpectedly, after returning home, the defendant intensified and severely beat her before imprisoning her in a room. Later, the neighbors heard about it and helped her out. According to the civil law on kinship, there is no concubinage system. All bigamy or adultery and abuse are conditions for divorce. Moreover, the cause of divorce is that one party can request future alimony in accordance with the precedents of the former Dali Court and the current civil law on kinship, which should also be borne by the defendant. Yesterday, Judge Chen Bingxin opened the court for mediation. The petitioner did not arrive, and her agent, lawyer Yao, arrived to interrogate. Yan A-Wu confessed that he was 24 years old, a local and lived in Yanjiachun, and was currently an apprentice at HSBC Bank. He has been married for six years. (Question) The petitioner requested a divorce and alimony of 4,000 yuan and a dowry of 1,800 yuan. What do you think? (Answer) I don't want to divorce. (Question) Do you still have a woman at home? (Answer) Yes, she taught me to marry her. (Question) What is this woman's name? (Answer) Her name is Chen Sanyuan and she is nominally a concubine. (Question) Do you live together? (Answer) Yes. (Question) Do you beat her? (Answer) I don't beat her. I go out to do business during the day and she takes the clothes back to her mother's house, such as a pair of gold bracelets, four gold rings, a gold hair clip, a gold lock, a gold chain, etc., weighing more than seven taels, and more than 500 yuan. (Question) Are you saying that she ran away with these things? (Answer) Yes. At this point, lawyer Yao rose to say that the petitioner is a pockmarked face, which is inevitable and not beautiful, so she does not please the defendant. So the defendant took the petitioner's gold ornaments one after another, but the Chen Sanyuan who is now married is very beautiful. The two are increasingly disliked in comparison. Please the court to investigate. The judge announced that he would summon and verify further.

Public Concession

Car Dealers' Emergency Meeting

Yesterday (the 28th), the Shanghai Municipal人力車 Guild's Special District Office held an emergency meeting for car dealers at the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association. 278 attendees, including Gu Songmao, Liang Ruiting, Liu Shengwu, Yin Zhiling, Hou Shao'an, Liu Zhenqiu, Cao Shuntai, Liu Ganquan, Lu Detai, Chen Shaoyun, etc., elected a presidium composed of Gu Songmao, Liang Ruiting, Bao Guoxiang, Yin Zhiling, Liu Shengwu, and Hou Shao'an, with Chen Yongsheng as the recorder. The meeting proceeded as scheduled. (A) Matters Reported: (1) Gu Songmao reported that the工部局's (Municipal Council) Carriage Office had notified them that, according to a board resolution, old, young, and visually impaired rickshaw pullers would be banned. If the car owners did not rectify the situation, the 工部局 would take strict measures and revoke their licenses. Yesterday, Comrade Hou Shao'an and I went to the 工部局 to discuss various matters with Director Fei, who advised us to hold a meeting of car dealers, gather opinions, and then discuss the ban. We hope that everyone will jointly decide. (B) Matters Resolved: (1) The age of rickshaw pullers should be between 17 and 50, with physical strength as the standard. (2) Visually impaired rickshaw pullers are absolutely prohibited. (3) If a rickshaw puller violates regulations, the license should not be confiscated; only the rickshaw puller can be detained and fined. (4) The appointment of the director of the Special District Office is ratified. (5) Reported to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce that the capital for each rickshaw should be 90 yuan. After discussion, Yin Zhiling, Hou Shao'an, Gu Songmao, and six others were nominated as representatives to attend the 工部局 meeting. The meeting adjourned at 7:30 PM.

Shanghai County Plans to Build Puxi Telephone

Total Line Length: 92 Li

The Puxi telephone project planned and constructed by the Shanghai County Construction Bureau was yesterday submitted to the county by Director Wu Wenhua along with the project proposal. The entire route consists of six sections: (1) From Beiqiao to Zhuanqiao, 6 li; (2) From Beiqiao to Minhang, 9 li; (3) From Beiqiao to Changqiao, connecting to the Shanghai urban area telephone network, 27.5 li; (4) From Beiqiao to Huajing, 22.5 li; (5) From Beiqiao to Tangwan, 10.5 li; (6) From Beiqiao to 认大 Yao Factory, 16.5 li. The total length is 92 li. Due to the county's financial difficulties, funding must be approved by the Provincial Construction Department. It is expected that funds will be raised from the province, county, and local communities. It is reported that the cost of materials and expenses for the Puxi section alone will be around 10,000 yuan.

Overview of the Continental Commercial Center's Layout

The Continental Bank is currently constructing the Continental Commercial Center at the corner of Nanjing Road and Shandong Road, and construction has already begun. The commercial center covers an area of six mu and has six floors. It faces Nanjing Road, Jiujiang Road, and Shandong Road on three sides. A T-shaped alley will be opened inside to connect the three roads. The alley will be three English feet wide and will have a parking lot for many cars. Sidewalks will be built on both sides of the alley. This alley will be named Buddha Street. Large elevators will be built at the three entrances, capable of lifting 120 people to each floor in one minute. Various shops will be built along the roads and alleys. The second floor will be used by the Continental Bank. The third and fourth floors and a portion of the second floor will have the latest and most novel equipment. Once the building is completed, a cooperative commercial center consisting of 300 shops will be established, with each shop conveniently displaying its goods. The fifth and sixth floors will have more than 100 large and small office spaces. A garden, dance hall, restaurant, club, cinema, and miniature golf course will be built on the roof. It is reported that several stores have already secured rooms in the commercial center, and it is expected that all floors will be fully occupied within the year.

Wang A'mei

Lawsuit over Xue's Estate Lost

The woman Wang A'mei previously retained lawyer Pan Cheng'e to represent her in the civil court of the French Concession, claiming that the plaintiff was the concubine of the late paint merchant Xue Bao'run. After living together, they had a daughter named Bao'bao. Since Xue's death, no one has provided for her, and she requested that Xue's estate be divided according to the law. Xue's wife, Sun, Xue's sons Jia Sheng, Yan Sheng, Gan Sheng, and Gen Sheng, also retained lawyer Lin Yingqing to represent them. After repeated summonses, arguments were finally heard and a ruling was awaited. Yesterday, the date of the ruling arrived, and both parties were summoned. Judge Gong announced the ruling, stating that in the case of the dispute between the two parties over the division of property, after the court's review, the ruling is as follows: "Ruling:" The plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed, and the litigation costs are borne by the plaintiff. The court order for provisional attachment is revoked. "Facts:" The dispute between the two parties in this case should first be based on the plaintiff's identity. As for whether Xue Bao'run made a will before his death, and whether the will was made before the implementation of the Inheritance Section of the Civil Code, these two points must be considered after the plaintiff's identity is determined. Now, the plaintiff claims to share the inheritance obtained by the defendants as Xue Bao'run's daughter. The defendants not only deny that she is Xue Bao'run's daughter but also state that her legal representative is not her biological mother, which is supported by evidence. The plaintiff has not presented any evidence and has not requested the summoning of any witnesses, relying only on two photographs as evidence of her mother-daughter and father-daughter relationship. How can this be considered sufficient? Confirming identity has a significant impact on individuals and families. How can photographs be the only evidence to determine identity? Since the plaintiff's identity cannot be verified, there is no doubt that she is not Xue Bao'run's daughter. How can she share the inheritance with the defendants? In summary, the ruling is made as stated in the main text.

Municipal Public Works Bureau Relief

Water Shortage in Xiangyan Bridge, Jiyang Lane

Urging Owners to Install More Public Faucets

There are twenty street-facing shops and sixteen lane houses, with about a hundred households, in Jiyang Lane, Xiangyan Bridge, Zhabei. Initially, they used well water, but due to the unclean water quality, the rent was increased by one yuan per month for each building to use tap water, with two public faucets installed. Later, the owners wanted to increase the rent again due to excessive water bills, but the tenants refused. As a result, one of the faucets was removed. In March of this year, residents of the lane requested the restoration of the removed faucet due to insufficient water supply, but the owners refused. They then reported to the Municipal Health Bureau, which forwarded the matter to the Municipal Public Works Bureau for handling. The bureau investigated and confirmed the situation and ordered the owners to install a public faucet for drinking water. The owners argued that after the installation of tap water faucets, tenants were using the water excessively, and the 粉皮 (rice noodle sheets) shop at No. 158 and the 大饼 (large pancake) wholesale shop at No. 155 were consuming even more water due to their business operations. How could they bear the huge water bills? They requested to be exempted from installing additional faucets. The bureau then informed the owners that the water used by the 粉皮 shop, etc., was for business purposes and that the shop should install its own meter for water usage. As for the water fees for the other households, which were included in the rent, the faucet should be installed quickly to ensure sufficient supply. However, the owner has delayed in doing so, and the residents have been complaining. Yesterday, it was learned that the Public Works Bureau ordered the owner, Wu Zhongyang, to install another faucet by the end of this month and notified the residents that if the owner fails to comply by the deadline, the residents can install it themselves and deduct all expenses from the rent. However, those whose water usage is for business purposes must install their own water meters to ensure fairness.

New Slaughterhouse to be Built on Dixiwei Road

According to the 大美晩报 (Shanghai Evening Post), the new slaughterhouse being built by the 工部局 Engineering Department on Dixiwei Road has already started construction. It covers an area of fourteen mu and costs 1,349,500 taels. After completion, it will be able to slaughter 970 cattle, 900 sheep, 300 pigs, and 300 calves per day, more than double the capacity of the existing Pelun Road slaughterhouse. According to last year's statistics, a total of 46,990 cattle, 46,000 sheep, 10,000 calves, and 25,000 pigs were slaughtered in the Public Concession. Therefore, the new slaughterhouse buildings are planned to be built in two stories, with the remaining two stories reserved for future expansion.

Wang Yongsheng's Whereabouts Unknown

Wang Yongsheng, who runs the Beiyang Hotel in Ning'an Lane, west of the North Railway Station, left alone on the morning of the 23rd of last month and sent a letter to his wife claiming suicide. More than a month has passed, and his whereabouts are still unknown. His wife, Fu, and children are crying day and night, in extreme distress. In addition to reporting to the Public Security Bureau to search for him, they hope that anyone who knows his whereabouts will notify them in order to reunite the family.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Yangtze River basin is cloudy and hot with thunderstorms. The coastal areas of the country are calm and windless. There is a cyclone in the Sea of Japan, moving east or northeast due to low pressure. The temperature in Shanghai for the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was a high of 90.5 and a low of 65.7. Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor,

I respectfully inform you that we have received a letter from Mr. Chen Zhuzhen of the Fucheng Company in Padang Serai, Kedah, Malaya, stating that his brother, Chen Qingji, previously studied at the Rili Minli Chinese School in the Dutch East Indies' Sumatra, but dropped out halfway. He went to Surabaya to do business for several years but was unsuccessful. He then stayed there for several months before returning to China to study, claiming to be studying at Jinan University. It has been three years since then, and there has been no news. He longs for family reunion and is saddened by the lack of news from the north. He wrote to us to inquire about his whereabouts, hoping for a reunion. We have checked the Jinan University registry and cannot find anyone named Chen Qingji. We admire your newspaper's enthusiasm for social welfare and its kindness in helping others. We have provided you with the details of the matter and respectfully request that you publish it in your newspaper so that he or his relatives can learn of his current situation and inform us so that we can forward it to him. We would be grateful, and not only we but also his elderly parents and young children across the ocean would be indebted to your newspaper and Mr. Editors.

Respectfully,

The Nanyang Cultural Affairs Department of National Jinan University

May 27, 1931

To Whom It May Concern:

I have read the article in your newspaper on the 27th regarding disputes over security deposits with our company. Our company is still in the preparation stage. If we officially open, we will first publish a statement. We have not dispatched the Dalong round trip Haizhou class, namely, the steamship crew, etc. Our company has nothing to do with it. How can there be a major dispute over a security deposit of 5,000 yuan? The He Wen Daily has already sent a letter requesting correction. We hereby send a letter to your newspaper office and request that you immediately correct it to clarify this matter.

Respectfully submitted to the Director of the Editorial Department of the 申報 Newspaper,

Zhuang Sheng, Manager, 大东轮船公司,

May 28th.
