World Snippets

—Hai Ke

A new law in Norway stipulates that doctors who write prescriptions with illegible handwriting will be fined.

The daughters and sisters of aviators at the Cranwell Aerodrome in Lincolnshire, England, have formed a new flying daughters team to conduct exercises.

The Bible is freely available in all countries except Soviet Russia.

The duties of port management have traditionally been performed by men and are not suitable for women. Recently, in England, Miss S. Gale has been elected as the port manager of Paignton Devon, at the age of only twenty-one.

Western Australia produces a black swan, commonly seen swimming in rivers, which is a beautiful sight. However, they have gradually become less common and may become extinct in the future.

Some hard-court tennis courts in London are sprinkled with salt before matches to absorb moisture from the air.

In India, a total of 25 million women are married before the age of sixteen, and 218,000 of them are under the age of five. There are also 396,556 widows under the age of fifteen.

The Eccentric Man on the Chimney

— Tao Zaidong

I have seen the eccentric man on the Japanese chimney twice. The first time was around January of this year. He stood on the chimney, neither eating nor drinking, for seven days before coming down. I called him a new-style Shen Baoxu. Recently, a 19-year-old dyer climbed the chimney due to an ineffective strike, breaking the previous record. Despite police persuasion and medical advice, he insisted on waiting for a satisfactory settlement before being lowered in a rope basket. All of these people harbored great aspirations and sacrificed their own interests, vowing to achieve their goals at all costs and placing themselves in extreme danger, as if hanging on the edge of a cliff. Since these events are rarely seen, the public regards them as eccentric. The newspaper criticized this action, saying that while it may not be unprecedented, it is certainly rare. Is it really rare? Tao Zaidong says no. In ancient times, there were no chimneys, but there were pagodas. Their solitary height and danger are equal to chimneys. Although Shen Baoxu cried for seven days without drinking a drop of water, he was still standing on flat ground, which is not worth mentioning. Yang Ruizhong's ascent of the Buddhist pagoda is also an eccentric act. Yang Ruizhong was from Zhending Prefecture in the Southern Song Dynasty. In November of the second year of Jianyan, the Jin people besieged Puzhou. Yang Ruizhong defended it. The Jin people attacked for thirty-two days. Yang Ruizhong climbed to the highest level of the pagoda from the northwest corner of the city. The city then fell. Yang Ruizhong did not descend when the Jin people called him. The Jin people, respecting his loyalty, promised not to kill him, and then he descended. The details are in the "Three Dynasties Northern Alliance Compilation," Volume 119. Comparing and criticizing, the object of the chimney is the Japanese, while the object of the pagoda is the Jin. The enemy of the gold cave is the Jin people. Are the events and people not even stranger? I once said that China's historical data is the richest. Except for electrical machinery, all events, large and small, trivial and bizarre, exist. The word "unprecedented" is not easy to say. Scholars of history should not be tired of reading more books.

A Celebration of the Du Ancestral Hall

— Lishan Nong

Mr. Du Yuesheng's public-spiritedness and righteousness are widely praised. Whenever various provinces appeal for disaster relief, he generously donates huge sums of money, cherishing Du Fu's desire for ten thousand rooms to shelter the poor and Bai Juyi's wish for a thousand-zhang-long quilt to keep them warm. He is not only surrounded by three thousand followers, rivaling Lord Mengchang of Qi during the Warring States period. Recently, he built an ancestral hall in Pudong to honor his ancestors and enlighten his descendants. The completion ceremony will be held on the fifth day of the second week of May. Friends from all over the country have sent gifts in advance, but Mr. Du has declined them all, only accepting poems and eulogies that can be kept as memorials. Yesterday, I passed by his residence and saw various treasures displayed in the hall, a dazzling array of beautiful objects. Commander-in-Chief Chiang and Deputy Commander-in-Chief Zhang personally inscribed plaques. Other important figures from the party, government, and military, as well as chambers of commerce from various provinces, all competed to offer couplets and poems, all of which were well-written and worthy of being passed down for generations. There were also gilded screen panels with vermilion silk borders, inscribed with Zhu Bolu's Family Instructions, mostly written by the writer Wang Xishen. In addition, Feng Yunchu and Wang Xishen sent a bronze stele with an inscription praising him: "Five hundred years of auspiciousness, the phoenix bird comes. Eleven clans of Shu Xiang, only the Yangshe remain. Black clothes and vermilion birds, the Wang and Xie families flourished in the Six Dynasties. Decorated carriages and red wheels, the Jin and Zhang families prospered in the Han Dynasty. The brilliance of the clan and the importance of the genealogy have always been valued. Since the world steals days and loses its order, the shrine of Tingjian is suddenly abandoned. The ancestors of Ruo Ao are finally hungry. Seeking fallen leaves on old branches, who can protect them? Asking for the same roots in different mounds, the Qiumu has no Yi 緦 hemp heart, and the children of the road. The elders who love their relatives sigh with emotion. Mr. Yuesheng, his clan is as high as the heavenly phenomena and his spirit is as strong as mountains and rivers. Continuing the ancestors of Rong, he cares for the descendants. Following the family spinning, he has a good model. Therefore, he built an ancestral hall in Kerry. The autumn frost and spring dew are originally Xie Gong's sincerity to stop the ancestors. He sees the love and hears the warning of Li's complete belonging. The spirits will always shine brightly and the spirit will be connected. Considering those who count their ancestors and forget their ancestors, they divination and get the surname, and the distant descendants ask Min Ziqian and do not know it. He continues Cui Wu, and he is even more ashamed. Is it not enough to encourage thin customs and promote Muhang? The Yao Yuan nine factions move the thinking of Longmen heaven. A branch of Guilin is like the spirit of the Lu Palace." The poems of praise are inexhaustible, and the etiquette is detailed in the washing and the offering. Dare to use this righteousness to make a eulogy. Said: "The houses are in pairs, and the poems are followed by Bai Ye. Strive to become Confucian heroes, save the time, and the clan hegemon. Describe virtue and inscribe meritorious deeds, and expand the mansion. The sun of love rises in the hall, and the clouds are rising in the hall. The Mao and Chong shades are spread, and the Shengge Sanya filial piety is practiced in auspicious order. The Shilu Qianyi respects the ancestors. The pictures of paintings show the brilliance of Wenyi. The brilliance of Lin Zhao at night rests, the east of Pupu admires the Gui Xian community. The Yunzhang Xian scale, the dew is scattered, and the musk is respectfully offered. At the time of summer, the Fen Cui is attached, and the words of the mint are arranged. The algae are scattered, and the regular script is beautiful. It is the most refined of the small works, and it is also written by Xishen." I heard that his disciples are also planning to raise more than 100,000 yuan to build a library next to the ancestral hall to help the development of culture and promote the popularization of education. The sound of iron zithers and copper swords will follow the ancients, and one day Jiangsu Province will have another famous site.

Detailed Account of Curing Snake Poison

— Fang Shen'an

Recently, in the "Free Talk" section of the 申報 Newspaper on May 18th, there was an article titled "Discussion of the Diagnosis and Treatment of Difficult Diseases," which was written by Mr. Ban Kuang, describing my medical cases of curing various difficult and strange diseases in recent years. One of the cases mentioned a woman suffering from 中蛊, whom I cured with a single needle, causing her to vomit poisonous snakes. This article was not detailed enough, so I am supplementing it to let readers know that all kinds of strange and difficult diseases can be cured using the old acupuncture methods passed down in China for 5,000 years, and there is often an unexpected effect. The patient was an elderly woman from Guangdong Province who said that she had been suffering from chest and abdominal pain for seven years. When the pain occurred, her face turned pale and she wanted to die but could not. She could only eat a small amount of beef and mutton to temporarily relieve the pain. She had been treated by many Chinese and Western doctors, but without any effect. I diagnosed her pulse as being large and small, slow and rapid, changing in an instant, and her complexion was also sometimes green and sometimes white, changing from time to time. I knew that her illness was not caused by ordinary abdominal masses or all kinds of stomach cold and stagnation. Moreover, since she was from Guangdong, where the harm of 中蛊 is often present, her pulse and complexion were both signs of worm disease. I guessed that her chest and abdominal pain was probably caused by 中蛊. Therefore, I used a large needle to penetrate deeply into the Zhongwan acupoint. Unexpectedly, as soon as the needle was inserted, the pain became unbearable. After a short while, she vomited a small amount of greenish water, which had an unbearable odor. After a while, a small snake wriggled out of her mouth, becoming longer and longer. The entire body was two feet long. After moving for about ten minutes, it died. An inch away from the snake's head was a wound, which was where I had inserted the needle. After the snake came out, not only did the pain stop immediately, but her chest and abdomen also felt comfortable and she thanked me sincerely. I used fire and alcohol to soak the Gu in a glass bottle and took a photograph to keep as a memento.

Complete Chinese Translation of the Quran Published

— Yong

Islam is prevalent in northwestern China, and there are many followers in Henan, Jinling, Jinan, etc. There are mosques throughout the country, which shows the breadth of its teachings. The Quran, consisting of thirty volumes, is followed, but it is passed down in Arabic. Not only are scholars unable to understand it, but even those within the religion may not be able to fully understand it. In the past, two masters, Liu Jielian and Ma Fuchu, made abridged translations, but they were not complete. Translations in English and Japanese are very prevalent, which makes the Chinese feel ashamed. Recently, Mr. and Mrs. Hardoon hired many talented individuals who were proficient in Islam to translate the Quran, which took three years to complete. The Quran now has a complete Chinese translation. It can not only rival the English and Japanese translations but also reveal the secrets of the past 1,300 years to the Chinese people and those within the religion. The entire book consists of 6,666 verses, covering doctrines, rules, history, and myths. In short, much of it is unknown to the people of China. Its benefits to the religion are self-evident. Even politicians, religious figures, historians, and philosophers can use it to understand the essence of the ancient sages and the broad and profound teachings. The publication of this complete edition can truly be called enlightening the teachings. The entire book is in eight volumes and includes prefaces and postscripts by famous people, which can serve as a guide for scholars. I believe that the book will spread far and wide on its own.

Around the Yellow Sea (16)

— Huang Yanpei

A friend of mine took office as the magistrate of a certain county in Zhejiang and asked me to give him a few words. I, never being one to be polite, gave him a long lecture: "There are three types of officials. The first is called '官' (official), the second is called '官官' (official-official), and the third is called '民官' (people's official)."

What is called "官"? "This person is full of official air." "Congratulations on your promotion and fortune." This may be what Zuo Zongtang said. "Can't you even be an official?" This is called "官," and it's everywhere, so I don't need to say more.

What is called "官官"? That is a higher level. He really wants to do things for the government and may be very good at doing things for the government. Every power that the government should have is taken over one by one. Every penny that the government should have is taken over, even if it is not supposed to have it, as long as the power of the government can get it, he will unceremoniously take it all over. He is a loyal minister of the officialdom, he is a loyal servant of the government. In his heart and eyes, there is only one 民府 (people's government) because he is an official of the government, so he is called "官官."

As for the third type, 民官, that is very different. In his heart and eyes, there are only the people. He only knows how to do things for the people. So the previous type should be called an official's servant, while he should be called a public servant. The previous type should be called 官官, while he should be called 民官.

You certainly won't be a "官," but will you be a "官官" or a "民官"? Please choose for yourself, my friend. This is all what I said to my friend.

When I arrived in Japan and saw how they worked in the officialdom, a fourth type of official appeared, which is called "国民" (national citizen). They completely do things for the country but are not official servants, nor are they worthy of being called public servants. They should only be called "国僕" (national servant).

Next to the desks of all their civil and military officials are large maps of Manchuria and Mongolia. When they are silent for a few minutes, they are all thinking about Manchuria and Mongolia, which are the future of our country.

On both sides of the street, the entrances to trams and public buses are very large, and advertisements are prominently displayed: "The Railway Bureau is launching a Manchuria-Mongolia sightseeing tour. The departure date, the return date, the places visited, the discount on fares, and other preferential treatment are listed, limited to a certain number of people. Sign up quickly!" This is a common occurrence, not an accidental one.

"Manchuria-Mongolia Affairs Lecture Topic (1) Observing Soybeans from the Perspective of Manchurian-Mongolian Resources (2) The Importance of Manchuria-Mongolia and Japanese Diplomacy Sponsor: [Name of Association] Supporter: [Name of Government Office]" This is what I saw in the countryside.

The tram safety movement was launched nationwide, with large advertisements posted everywhere: "April 20th to 26th is the Tram Safety Period. Absolutely no accidents are allowed. It is hoped that all employees will work together to achieve this. Sponsor: Transportation Administration Office." This is our nation's moment of rights! This is our nation's moment of glory! A group of national officials are imagining this. Our country's administrative organs are too busy. How can they manage this kind of national affair?

Rotary Club

The Future World (2)

— Tian Xuwo Sheng

The first time, I used fluorite and sulfuric acid to make frosted glass, but it was easy to get dirty and troublesome to clean. The second time, I used fluorite and bone ash to make opaque milky white porcelain, but it was still easy to get dirty, and it looked like a baker's shop. Finally, I added cobalt oxide to make opaque blue, which I found satisfactory. It was even more beautiful than Indanthrene-dyed fabrics. As for the cost, it was extremely cheap. Each vat of glass material cost only twelve yuan, but it weighed four hundred pounds. Each pound cost only four cents, which was cheaper than paper. At first, I used cottonseed hulls instead of coal. But when I made a large batch of potassium glass and then a batch of lead glass, I first used a press to press them into round table-sized convex glass. I used sunlight to capture the sun's heat to burn the glass, which didn't cost a penny. Because clothes made of soft glass threads are not easily torn, if they are damaged, they only need to be returned to the furnace without needing potassium carbonate again. Therefore, cottonseed hulls were also eliminated. Moreover, I don't like social engagements, so I don't need to constantly change my clothes. Therefore, crucibles, presses, convex lenses, etc. were also eliminated. Isn't this solving the problem of clothing? As for the problem of food, I watched a movie about the new world fifty years later and looked up the "Emergency Relief Method" in Volume Sixteen of "Verification of New Prescriptions." It said that only glutinous rice, sesame, and red dates are needed to make pills, each weighing five qian. Taking one pill a day can prevent hunger for a day. It was originally very cheap, but it still seemed troublesome to make and eat. So I changed to the method of Baopuzi, which only involves touching the tip of the tongue to the upper palate every morning to produce saliva in the mouth. Swallow it slowly in dozens of mouthfuls several times in a row. This can gradually reduce hunger. At first, you can stop eating breakfast. Gradually, you can swallow this Huachi saliva no matter where you are, sitting or lying down. It has actually become a Taoist habit of 服氣 (breathing exercises). Therefore, you don't eat and you don't get hungry. So not only is the problem of food solved, but the problem of drink is also solved at the same time. Therefore, I have no dregs in my chest and no need for excretion. Tap water, fire, and toilets, chamber pots, rice bowls, tea cups, etc. are also completely eliminated. Because my residence has saved many cumbersome things and I am accustomed to meditation, practicing the "gentleman enters rest" rule, I don't need a bed. It's not meditation, nor is it a single-lotus or double-lotus sitting position. Just casually bending your arms and resting your head, or leaning on a table and lying down, can nourish your spirit. It's truly like a dragon horse, and even better than a dragon horse. Although the dragon horse doesn't close its eyes to sleep, it still needs to roll over. I don't need to roll over. I only need to rest for a while and I'm fine. So there is only one table and one chair in the house, which is enough to accommodate me. A square zhang room already feels large and inappropriate. In fact, only a mat is enough. At first, I wanted to build a castle in the air because I had to wait fifty years before there were air police. I was afraid that an airplane would crash into me. I thought that if an airplane crashed into the mast of a sand boat, the airplane would break, but the sand boat would not capsize. It's better to live in a boat. So I used a pontoon boat as a base, with glass windows on three sides and a brick wall made of magnesium cement on one side. I used louvered windows instead of rafters and tiles. I closed them when it rained and opened them when I wanted wind. It's really interesting on a beautiful spring and autumn day. Zhang Zhihe's floating home is a good method.

Business News

Finance

Gold Market Plunges After Peak

Falls Back 14.9 Taels

Dramatic Fluctuations: Yesterday, the 28th, spot gold prices experienced a strong shift from a peak to a slump. The intense volatility was chaotic and uncontrollable. Price swings of several taels were common, totaling over 24 taels throughout the day, culminating in a sharp drop of 15 taels. Industry players were bewildered. Overall, large holders aggressively sold off, reversing the previous surge. This massive change was hardly unexpected; the silver market decline immediately opened higher, then surged to 812 taels, breaking yesterday's new record. Subsequently, foreign exchange remained tight despite a slight reduction in quotations. The aggressive selling by Dahing, Yongyuan Hing, and Yong Hing, among others, was unaffected. It is rumored that the Central Bank and Yu Feng Yong, along with other bullish entities, were offloading their positions, forcing the market environment into a tempestuous situation. After a catastrophic plunge of over 10 taels, the price dramatically broke through 800 taels, leading to further market weakness and widespread panic, plummeting to below 790 taels. Selling pressure remained intense, almost leading to a complete collapse. The foreign exchange situation further deteriorated, causing a standstill in cash flow. Holders were eager to liquidate, significantly impacting futures.

New High Price Achieved: Since the market opened in early July, the price had increased by 5 taels and 1 mace to 809 taels, due to a substantial drop of one-eighth in silver prices and a simultaneous one-quarter drop in public and private telegram rates. Qian Industry Market Changes Meeting Time

The qian industry market has traditionally started its meetings and mutual market trading at 8:30 every morning and 12:30 at noon, as well as setting silver interest rates, foreign interest rates, and other market prices. Now, because the days are long and the nights are short, there is a need to advance the morning meeting time. Therefore, it was decided yesterday by the market committee to start the silver interest rate meeting at 8:00 every morning starting from June 1, half an hour earlier than usual, while the noon market will remain the same.

Kinué Hitomi and the Marriage Question

— Fu Lan

Speaking of the name of the Japanese Miss Kinué Hitomi, it is truly like thunder in the ears; the whole world knows it. Unexpectedly, yesterday, Reuters in Tokyo reported that she is suffering from severe meningitis. Even if she recovers, she may be forced to no longer actively participate in sports because her weak health cannot cope. This news will surely attract public attention and regret.

However, Miss Hitomi currently has a more personal and lifelong matter that has not been resolved, which may be reducing her interest in sports. She is already twenty-five years old this year. At this age for women in Japan, if they have not yet obtained a husband, they will begin to feel anxiety. Miss Hitomi herself has truthfully acknowledged this situation in an article published in Osaka in the "New Society for Women, May Issue."

In this article, Miss Hitomi says that it is not just the fact that she is twenty-five that makes her anxious. What she dislikes most is that curious friends often ask her questions, which annoys her. She says, "People often ask me when I plan to get married. My answer is 'I don't know.' Maybe I will never get married, although I want to reserve this thought. Because once I become a real old maid, or if I change my mind, some people will surely remember what I said now and secretly laugh at me."

In the past, the main questions Miss Hitomi's friends and admirers asked her whenever they met were, "Do you exercise every day?" and "What record do you plan to break at the next World Games?" But recently, these questions have been abandoned, replaced by "Are you still exercising?" and "But, of course, you must be thinking about getting married, right?"

In this article, Miss Hitomi also said, "Senior colleagues often advise me to start considering marriage, but I often honestly ask myself if my nature is suitable for marriage. Marriage is asking for trouble because it can sometimes make people stupid and rob them of their enterprising spirit. I don't want to consider this kind of marriage. It's just that people often bring up the question to advise me, and some even ridicule me, saying that I am a famous athlete who, when she gets angry, will take it out on her husband and beat him. But I never think of doing such a thing because my heart is not cruel. As for the fierce look on my face when I race, that is irrelevant."

"So, putting aside the thought of marriage, I want to find something I can do. If I devote the time I spend considering marriage to my work, of course, I can achieve great things."

Miss Kinué Hitomi has been to Europe three times to attend competitions and has won many international women's championships. Among the most famous are the 200 meters (24.7 seconds) in 1929 and the 400 meters (59 seconds) in 1928, both of which were women's records she created.

Marshal Foch's World War Diary

— Translated by Gu Angruo

An examination of the temporary setbacks of the German attack and the situation created by the reinforcement of the Allied forces south of the Somme River, as well as the conclusions drawn from relevant enemy intelligence, are as follows:

(1) The enemy, who is blocked between the Scarpe River and Arras, may be able to launch another attack. His re-attack will be difficult south of the Somme River, but easier to start north of the Somme River. Therefore, a particularly strong line of defense should be set up between the Somme River and Arras. This is the work undertaken by the British General Headquarters. The French reserve forces gathered in the Beauvais area should be able to move to the north of the Somme River to fight. The procedures for transporting troops must be arranged in advance. This is the problem of the French General Headquarters.

(2) Regardless of the German strategy, our army should quickly preemptively strike south of the Somme River in order to drive the enemy away from the Paris-Amiens railway and the center of the Amiens railway, because these two places are extremely important for our army's transportation and supply. According to this policy, the military law aims to drive the enemy to Roye. An offensive should be launched immediately in the Montdidier area. The British army aims to relieve the danger of Amiens and should attack simultaneously on both sides of the Somme River.

From then on, the Allied forces switched to the offensive. The completely passive attitude since March 21 and the solid defense work forced by the situation came to an end, replaced by an active offensive.

Now, planning the offensive battle, encouraging the soldiers, directing the battle, urging the two general commands to coordinate everything, and allocating forces, the power given to me by the Doullens Agreement is clearly insufficient. Even in directing the current offensive battle, I feel stretched. Soon, the American army will join the war, and my responsibility is to arrange the coordination of the Allied forces. According to the situation, the evaluation criteria for each army's attack, the allocation of offensive and defensive work, and the alternation of French and Italian troops at the front will be determined. My authority will definitely feel even more constrained.

The simple task of the coordinator is not enough for the larger plans that are about to be carried out. If he wants to react quickly and forcefully to unexpected events in the defensive war or launch a large-scale offensive, he has little room to maneuver. His task should be changed to that of commander. If the Doullens Conference created this Allied mechanism out of trust, its power should be immediately expanded and entrusted with full authority to command the Western Front war, acknowledging that its authority is higher than that of the Allied general commands. The front-line troops from the North Sea to the Adriatic Sea must be completely under its control.

A few days of experience have been enough to expose the shortcomings of the Doullens Agreement. The current and future interests of the Allied forces urgently require the revision of this agreement. I, therefore, raised this issue to the French Prime Minister based on this intention and requested that the decisions of the British and French governments regarding me on March 26 be supplemented. Clemenceau discussed this matter with me on April 1 and decided to convene another new meeting. He then invited representatives from the United States, Britain, and France to attend this meeting. Two days later, on April 3, a resolution was passed at the Beauvais City Hall as follows:

"The British, French, and American governments entrust General Foch with the task of coordinating the Western Front Allied forces and grant him full authority to command the war." (To be continued)
